Common Sense Ethical Views and YAMAMOTO Yūzō 204

— Zhang Xiangshan

Because of the play "Infanticide", Yamamoto Yūzō has become a very well-known playwright in our country. In fact, Yamamoto Yūzō is also a very outstanding figure among Japanese playwrights.

In Japan, those who can be called playwrights are indeed as rare as morning stars. People like Kubota Mantarō, Yoshii Isamu, Masamune Hakuchō, Tanizaki Jun'ichirō, and the one-act play expert Kikuchi Kan are mostly novelists or poets. Those who can truly be called playwrights are only Okamoto Kido, Kishida Kunio, and Yamamoto Yūzō. Among them, the existence of Okamoto Kido is still half based on feudal kabuki, while Yamamoto Yūzō is different. He inherited the naturalistic atmosphere of the Taishō era, focusing on the expression of realistic daily life. Because his plays have a tight structure, he has received very good reviews. Therefore, some people have commented that he is very similar to Ibsen, which is not an excessive evaluation.

His works can be said to be consistently interwoven with common sense ethical views. Because of this, he cannot escape the so-called superficial "sense of morality." He only uses this common sense ethical view to deal with and respond to the real society. Moreover, he can only discover the lack of this common sense ethical view in the current society, but he cannot go deeper to grasp the root of the problem. Taking the well-known "Infanticide" as an example, we can understand the full picture of Yamamoto Yūzō's common sense ethical view.

The story of "Infanticide" is as follows: A policeman named Koyama, due to poverty, was unable to treat his wife and son's illnesses, and they eventually died. Thus, he lived a life of hardship with his daughter. At this time, he deeply felt that his wife and son's deaths were caused by himself because he did not have the money to treat them.

At this time, a female worker who pulls earth killed and buried her own baby, but it was eventually discovered. Later, this woman came to Koyama to plead her case. Koyama angrily rebuked her for harming an innocent life, wanting to tie her up and beat her. But after the woman explained that in order to support her family, she had to kill the baby who was hindering her from working, and that she thought it was better for the child to die than to suffer in the world, he showed great sympathy and comforted her, saying: "In court, this crime may be leniently punished depending on the circumstances."

From the above story, we can see several significant facts. First, the character Koyama is the entire representative of Yamamoto Yūzō's thoughts, that is, full of a strong ethical view and sense of morality. Second, the female worker's killing of the baby is a very common sense event. Third, the current society's laws still protect these poor people.

The author's depiction of the central character Koyama, his deep love for his dead wife and children, his loyalty to his duties, his gentle heart towards his daughter, and his initial anger towards the criminal followed by comfort, can be said to be a picture of the kindest and most moral human being. However, whether this kind of human being truly exists in this world is a major question. Needless to say, this is the author's ideological construction, trying to concretely express many abstract common sense ethical views in this character.

As for the common phenomenon of infanticide, it is an extraordinary fact. Although Yamamoto Yūzō recognized the impropriety of this society that produces such tragedies, he still adhered to maintaining the morality of the current society's laws. While Ibsen's problem plays raise many questions, they also hold suspicion and distrust towards the current society. However, Yamamoto Yūzō is different. He only writes about some unreasonable tragedies in this society, but he still believes that society can be rationalized, and he still believes in the existence of characters constructed by his ethical views.

Here, we might as well use "Crown of Life" as an example. The general plot of this play is as follows: A merchant who runs a crab meat canning factory accepts a direct order from England, thus arousing the jealousy of intermediary traders. They start to disrupt their crab production by having crab fishermen raise crab prices, causing the factory to lose money. So the factory owner's younger brother decides to buy cheap crabs such as small crabs and female crabs to mix in, in order to avoid losses. However, the older brother absolutely refuses to do this kind of deceptive behavior, because he believes that it is detrimental to the merchant's morality and the commercial reputation of Japan. As a result, he resolutely buys expensive crabs, leading to bankruptcy, and leaves the house and factory that have already been sold to others with his sick wife, younger brother, and sisters.

This is a tragedy, the downfall of a person who faithfully adheres to common sense morality. Needless to say, in the author's intention, it is an attack on the hypocrisy and evil of the current world, but at the same time, he still believes in: "Those who can maintain eternal honesty, I can give them this glorious crown of life." This is also his belief in this ethical concept, that no matter what difficulties and failures are encountered, they can finally obtain this final crown of life. This kind of thinking constitutes the true life of Yamamoto Yūzō's plays, and at the same time, it also reveals Yamamoto Yūzō's backwardness.

Finally, I must point out the advantages of his plays and his method. What are his advantages and method? He can observe a phenomenon from various angles, and knows how to grasp an event as a combination of various relationships. He can see a complex structure from simple things, and knows that daily life contains more meaning than extraordinary things. This can be understood by reading his novel, "Wave." Another point is the tight structure of his plays. This tightness brings about the overall effect of his plays.

As for his other works, there are "Comrades," Professor Tsuda, etc. His novel "A Woman's Life" has also received very good reviews. This novel has some similarities with Maupassant's "A Woman's Life." Needless to say, the strength of Maupassant's "A Woman's Life," according to Tolstoy, is that it has first: the author's proper relationship with the subject matter, that is, a moral relationship. Second, the expression is accurate and beautiful (these two are consistent). Third, honesty, in other words, a genuine feeling of love for the subject matter taken. Yamamoto Yūzō's "A Woman's Life" also gained considerable prestige because of its emphasis on moral relationships and the use of the naturalistic method. But according to Teshima Tetsuzo, "The success of this novel is half due to the harvest of transplanting the tight writing method of his plays into the novel."

Ant Life 205

— Ling Mo

It is probably worthy of getting mocked to pity for the life of a fly. In reality, I myself also don't forget that old story: a summer cicada, happily singing songs from a tree branch, not hurrying, while an ant is busily working under the hot sun. In winter the ant survives off of its preserved stores of grain, while the cicada starves to death on the road. Thus, the cicada's death is not only lighter than a feather, it is plainly so light it can't even compare to its own wings. The meaning of this lesson is to teach us that the cicada's death is deserved. However, I feel that putting this great effort into explaining that it's not a pity for the cicada to die, in the end we are still taking this death too seriously. In reality, it is that ant that is praised in the story, and from the human's perspective, its death is also just a small ant life.

Though in the mood of creating a fable, at times even flower and grass, wood and stone, are endowed with a life, people are always possessing the desire of exclusively occupying the function of life. With one more thing possessing life in the universe, a person knows that their own privileged rights to enjoy have suffered one more level of stripping. Because of that, humans are constantly doing the work of denying the life of others, destroying the life of others, and despising the life of others. And micro-organisms are the most despised; they are diminished to the furthest extent, so in the eyes of a hunter, no matter flying bird or running animal, they are all just a few bugs. All of this is life worthy of scorn, that is worth being exterminated. Of course, there are also those who fret that if the world reaches a day when besides humans there aren't any other forms of life, that it will be an extremely boring world. But those living in cities where there aren't fierce beasts and aren't scorpions and snakes intruding, probably all hope that in the future there won't even be a single fly or a single bed bug. Though that is just the attitude towards the life we can despise, and towards life worthy of admiration, it is naturally not completely the same. However, the difference is really just a limit; mankind towards life that is completely under its control, is not acknowledging the existence of that life, and is already prepared to destroy it at any time upon discovering that it is loathsome.

Mankind has built up ten-thousand years of the history of destroying life of other forms, and in the present there is still much life that exists and has not been destroyed, and that can only be said to be by chance. These lives are only able to exist, because the steps that mankind takes are pretty chaotic; humans themselves do not know that humans are just other humans. Everyone takes themselves to be the ones surviving after the flood, and that their own survival is from having admirable nature, while those bearing sins, can only be destroyed in the flood. The hope for the world to have another flood, is hidden within the heart of just a certain portion of people, and that is without question. There are even some people that simply hope to possess divine-like power and to transform the world all over once. The so-called world culture from before the European War, and today the current catchphrase of "pure Aryan bloodlines", are all containing the danger that a portion of humanity will be destroyed. Comparing to the facts of the past, knowing all of this is not an absurd worry. In the past there were many human deaths that substituted for the killing of bugs and ants, and even today, there are some who are even fantasizing that humanity will probably bring its own total annihilation, so that the future world will be the ant world.

Here I am not at all intending to say that humankind should abandon their self-destructive actions, or using all its strength to fight against ants. The conjecture that the future is the world of ants, after all, is just a fable. In fables there are often lessons, but the lessons are often not necessarily good. The old fables compared to new fables, are in reality the same, they indicate to the people how to maintain their lives. Humans in reality have already become overly familiar with this, and that is why when straying upon a considerably distant fork in the road, returning to the starting point does not necessarily prevent a re-straying onto the same fork. Averting the self-destruction of humanity, or eliminating the psychology of despising other forms of life, are probably not necessary. Then do we believe in the old saying of all things breeding and growing along with me, not harming each other? Of course not, just not harming so that it is constantly annoying you.

In Memory of a Lost Child 206

— Ye Zi

A month ago, when my hometown was completely submerged, I received letters from both my sister and my wife's family, reporting that there was a severe epidemic raging there. Nine out of ten children were suffering from malaria and dysentery, and unfortunately, my son had also been infected. They wanted me to quickly send money to pray to the gods and buy medicine, hoping for some improvement. The child's symptoms were: cold limbs, constant watery diarrhea, unfocused eyes, etc.

At the time, I didn't show the letters to my mother and wife, because they were both still ill. Moreover, I knew that with such symptoms in a flood, there was absolutely no hope of recovery.

I secretly hung my heart up! Behind my mother and wife's back, I ran around everywhere, looking for money everywhere. Sometimes, I would hide away somewhere alone, facing the dim sky of my hometown, quietly, silently for a long time! Slowly, from those flying, floating wisps of clouds, I conjured up our vast village, houses, and fields. I saw thousands upon thousands of disaster victims, their bellies like leaves, lying on hard rocks! I saw animals drifting aimlessly! I saw the wailing of women and children! I saw the old and weak, those who couldn't withstand the torment, voluntarily, secretly crawling! Rolling! ... into the water.

I looked everywhere for my beloved son, but I couldn't see him. Was he dead? Or was he still among those sick, garbage-like, haggard crowds? I began to resent my eyes. I strained to open them wide! Wide! I wiped them with a towel! Finally, I couldn't see anything: dark clouds gathered from all directions, thunder and lightning intertwined, a huge, mountain-like black spot pressing down directly on my head.

As soon as my senses returned, I became even clearer: my child was undoubtedly beyond saving! Like the other disaster victims, he would have been lying on the hard rocks with his leaf-like belly, crying out to his cruel mother and heartless father!

I deeply regretted that I shouldn't have been so focused on the hardships of life, and so easily, so heartlessly left him alone in our hometown. What was happening now? What was happening? ... Ah! How could I ever erase the deep condemnation in my heart?

Perhaps there was still a chance! Send the money quickly! I thought to myself, trying to comfort myself. I tried my best to put on a calm and composed demeanor, and I didn't let my mother and wife know anything.

One afternoon, I went out to see a friend and was away from home for about three or four hours. It was already late when I returned. As soon as I entered the door, I heard a sharp, agonizing wail that pierced from my ears straight into my heart! I staggered and stood by the door. I knew that something extraordinary had already happened! My body trembled, almost shrinking into a ball!

My mother suddenly rushed out of the room, clutching my clothes! The sixty-three-year-old woman was like a drunk, her voice hoarse from crying! She cursed me as a heartless beast, only caring about my own life and not cherishing my children! She even said that I didn't tell her about the child's illness sooner. My wife was prostrate on the ground, holding the child's photo, spitting up black blood! My other daughter, who was already three years old, was also wailing in terror because of this sudden turmoil!

My eyes were blurred and confused! My breathing was rapid! My hot tears rolled down like a broken string of pearls! Ignoring their crying, I reached for the ominous letter on the table, soaked with tears and blood:

"... Died because there was no money for treatment! ... It was so pitiful, it was on the morning of the 27th of the seventh lunar month! ... Many children are dying here! ... Adults too! ... People here are living the lives of ghosts, walking the road to death day by day! ..."

My eyes went dark, and I couldn't see any more of the words.

Late at night, when their crying had subsided somewhat, I tried my best to bear the pain and quietly comforted my wife:

"What's the point of crying anymore? People like us, born into a world like this, shouldn't have children in the first place! If we have them, then they die! What good does crying do? Wouldn't the child suffer if he stayed with us? Isn't our hometown losing adults by the thousands? Hunger, disease! ... Look at all the blood and phlegm you just coughed up! ..."

My wife looked at me, biting her pale lips, her eyes red; despairingly, faintly, she said:

"Why? Why do we have to suffer like this? Our child! Our hometown! ..."

The Responsibility of Beauty (II) 207

Original by George Bernard Shaw, translated by Ting

—That is really bad. What have you endured? Don't say those pretty words to me. Please tell me straightforwardly. Having hired a lawyer with your money, you now have the privilege to tell him most of your private affairs. Don't remember that we are old friends, just remember that I am your lawyer. Besides, you don't need to say anything else to me. I have heard things like yours from the mouths of husbands sitting in that chair more than fifty times. Do you think you are the only one in the world who has disagreements with his wife?

—I can bet anything you like that you have never heard a case like mine. I can make it clear if you will let me know.

—Okay, then listen to me. Have you ever heard a woman say to her husband, "Nature has given her a special nature that makes people want to talk to her about love, but she considers it a sin and doesn't practice it"?

—That's because she wants you to talk to her about love.

—Yes: she has done that; and says it is so good, she has made me improve so much, and now she wants to keep doing it to make other people improve. She says it's like a talent for raising children. Any woman who has this talent, she says, is like running a school and providing education. They are so clever at this that they neglect their own children and pursue the children of others. In the same way, she argues, a woman should use that talented love to make people improve, should improve many, many more people. What do you think?

The lawyer felt a little sympathy and said:

—There's some truth in that, you know.

—What?

—Of course, I mean in terms of reason. Actually, that kind of thing is impossible; however, there's no malicious intent in it. Regarding this matter, I feel it's hard to find a suitable solution.

—That's what she said.

—Hey, so what did you say to her?

—I told her that the proper solution to this is: she herself should suffer.

—Did that do any good?

—No good at all.

—Does she dislike you already?

—No. She reports that she is willing to continue working with me, but she has become bored with me, so there must be a new interest growing in her life. Now, what do you say to your opponent?

—My opponent! Have I said a word for her?

Small Town 208

— Fei Er

The small town is piled full of old things, built with feudal relics.—A person who lives in a small town for a long time will get a musty smell all over them.

The people in the small town are short-sighted, they can't see things that are far away, they don't care about things outside their immediate surroundings. They are busy all day long for their families and lives, calculating trivial matters the size of a needle all day long.

The small town is just a lonely small town; it has nothing to do with the world, and it has nothing to do with all of humanity.

Only when one dog fights another dog in the small town, or when one pig gives birth to twelve piglets, will it be noticed by the townspeople.

Therefore, there is a local emperor in the small town, whose power exceeds that of any emperor in the world; therefore, there is also an eternal fool in the small town, whose fate is destined to be a stupid member who can never turn over.

The books that people in the small town read are "Laughing Grove Anecdotes," and those infected with modern airs read "The Analects"; the novels that people in the small town read are "Seven Swordsmen and Thirteen Knights," and the new-style talented scholars and beautiful ladies read "Tears and Laughter Marriage" or Zhang Ziping-style novels.

Occasionally, a gust of wind blows, and the small town is completely stirred up. Then there is unrest, disputes, fights, shootings, or even revenge, but after the wind blows, the small town returns to calm, like an ancient well that has been silent and waveless for thousands of years.

So the people in the small town are drilling in a narrow cave: like dung beetles, you crawl on my body, and I crawl on your body.

The crumbling frame of the small town is waiting for the second strong wind to blow, and it can all collapse.

During a short stay in the small town, I felt this way; I view all old small towns in the same way.

This doesn't mean that I'm praising big cities.

Shanghai Peiming Girls' Middle School Tenth Anniversary Special Issue

Foreword 209

— (Jin Yuezhang)

Time flies, and fleeting moments disappear like a flash of lightning. Since the establishment of our Peiming Girls' Middle School, it has been ten years in the blink of an eye! We are pleased to celebrate the grand anniversary, reflecting on the difficulties of creation in the past and planning for future development. We respectfully present a brief account of the school's administrative evolution over the past ten years to our fellow countrymen:

Regarding Facilities: The school's buildings have moved three times. When it was first established in the autumn of the fourteenth year, it rented a private house in Xinqiao East, Maigen Road, Shanghai, with only three floors. In the eighteenth year, it moved to No. 32, Maigen Road, Xinqiao West, which was slightly expanded but still insufficient. In the nineteenth year, another building was rented at No. 20, Wuding Road, for the elementary school. In the twentieth year, the Maigen Road site was expanded, and the elementary school was moved back. It was not until the twenty-second year that a new site was found at No. 210, Maigen Road, with its quiet gardens, spacious classrooms, large playground, and clean dormitories, providing a place for hundreds of students to rest, relax, and play. As for the internal improvements, there is also much to mention, such as the purchase of books, the addition of equipment, and the provision of school supplies, all of which are readily available. The exhibits displayed before the audience today are also quite impressive.

Regarding Staff and Students: At the beginning of the school year in the fourteenth year, there was only one class each in junior high and elementary school, with only forty students. The following year, one class was added to each department, and the number of students doubled. The year after that, senior high school was added, and the number of students increased even more. The school's grade levels were thus completed. From then on, the number of students entering the school increased year by year, reaching more than four hundred today. The number of teachers has increased from five or six to more than thirty, all of whom are graduates of specialized universities at home and abroad, enthusiastic about guidance and dedicated to teaching. All of the past staff members have been experienced, dedicated to their duties, and striving for the improvement of school affairs. Therefore, they have been able to cooperate, pool their wisdom and efforts, and jointly seek development, laying the foundation for today.

Regarding Student Achievements: The school's moral education has always been committed to cultivating a pure and simple academic style and developing a spirit of hard work. The school's policy is to carefully examine students' academic performance and to be particularly strict with their annual examinations, so the students are pure in character and excellent in academic achievement. They have won championships in city-wide speeches many times, and have also achieved excellent results in joint examinations. It is estimated that more than 40% of the graduates have been admitted to famous universities in China, and 50% are serving the community. All of this is statistically verifiable, and it is not difficult to find their names on the lists, so it has attracted the attention of people from all walks of life, who have praised it. How could we dare to expect such success?

Regarding Future Plans: Women's education in China has been established for more than forty years, and it has produced many talents. However, family life has not improved, and social customs are becoming increasingly decadent, causing the entire nation to be in a state of turmoil and unable to recover! Although there are many reasons for this, the inadequacy of the education system is an obvious fact. Scholars of the present age seek to revitalize the nation, so they advocate for productive education and seek immediate solutions, because future women must obtain correct knowledge and sound skills from education so that they can work together with men in social production and promote national economic development. In view of this, the school added a senior high school normal school class in the eighteenth year; four years later, a business class was added. Now that the normal school class should be returned to national conditions, it has been concluded; and the three-year business class has been completed. In the future, we plan to gradually expand agricultural and industrial vocational courses to the best of our ability, with the aim of creating productive talents for social application. This is the goal that we are aiming for in the future.

In summary, the school has established a relatively complete scale in a limited period of ten years. This is the result of the faculty and staff sacrificing their mental and physical strength and working diligently. Only then have we been able to receive social praise and assistance. Therefore, in the sixteenth year, the school board approved the registration with the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, and in the same year, it was approved for record by the Ministry of Education. The inspectors who have visited the school have found it satisfactory. In addition to the joy and encouragement on the anniversary, we must also think about how to strive for progress and contribute to society. As for the school's administrative organization and the curriculum of each level, they are all handled in accordance with the Ministry of Education's regulations, so we will omit them. We have described the major aspects of management in such detail.

Shanghai Peiming Girls' Middle School Tenth Anniversary

(A) Academics 214

1. Organization of Grade Levels

The school is divided into three departments: senior high, junior high, and elementary school. The senior high is further divided into business and general studies. There are three classes in junior high. The senior high business and general studies each have three grades, for a total of nine middle school classes. The elementary school has six grades and four classrooms. The junior high aims to suit the individual's profession and cultivate the level to enter senior high school. The senior high general studies focuses on entering university undergraduate programs. The business studies focuses on studying economic principles and cultivating practical commercial talents. The elementary school aims to cultivate good citizens and engage in primary occupations and enter junior high school.

2. Course Arrangement

The course arrangements for the junior high, senior high general studies, and elementary school at all levels all follow the Ministry of Education's curriculum standards for primary and secondary schools. As for the business course standards, the Ministry of Education has not yet stipulated them, so the school's business courses are mostly compiled and edited with reference to the courses offered by famous business schools in Shanghai.

3. Textbook Selection

The textbooks used in each grade, except for a part of the business courses and art courses that are edited by the school, are mostly textbooks approved by the Ministry of Education. However, when selecting textbooks, we try our best to ensure the connection and coordination of each subject and the improvement of teaching effectiveness. At the beginning and end of each semester, the academic affairs office must discuss with the teachers several times before making a decision.

4. Review of Homework

In addition to paying attention to lectures and exercises in class, the school also strictly reviews homework for each department and subject. Precise plans are made for each subject in advance. When the time comes to collect and review, there is no leniency. For example, the homework for the Chinese language subject includes four types: reading notes, composition notebooks, diaries, and calligraphy practice books. English, mathematics, science, business arithmetic, bookkeeping, and other subjects all have practice books. Moreover, the commercial subjects all have notebooks for review.

5. Performance Assessment

The school assesses student academic performance by combining three items: daily grades, monthly exams, and semester exams to determine the semester grade. Daily grades are based on the quality of the student's answers, exercises, and homework during class, as well as the quality of the production. The monthly exam time is designated by the academic affairs office to start and end within a certain week, and is held during class time. As for the semester exam at the end of the semester, the academic affairs office schedules the dates, assigns numbers, and conducts a comprehensive test of all the materials taught in a semester.

6. Self-Study Guidance

Every evening except Saturday, there are two hours of self-study, supervised and guided by the class teachers in each classroom. Important teachers of each subject are also invited to stay overnight at the school to facilitate students' inquiries at any time.

7. Attendance Statistics

In order to assess the progress of student performance, the school attaches great importance to the method of collecting student attendance statistics. Every day, the teachers in charge of the class take attendance every period, and report the names of absent students to the class teachers after class. At the end of each week, the academic affairs office uses this to fill out a form to compare the diligence of each grade. Students with excessive absences are given counseling or punishment at any time.

8. Speech Training

The school attaches great importance to public speaking. Every other week, prominent figures from society are invited to the school to give speeches for observation. Every other week, a speech contest is held, with several people drawn by lot each time. They practice in advance, and the two or three winners are determined at the time. At the end of each semester, a final competition is held. Therefore, students who have been at the school for half a year can speak Mandarin and express their opinions to the public. They have also won various important speech competitions in Shanghai, and have been praised by people in Shanghai.

9. Importance of Current Events

In order to encourage students to pay attention to reading newspapers and closely follow international news and national administration, each week the class teachers take turns explaining the main points and significance of the week's important current events during the memorial week. A current events test is held once each semester, divided by grade, with grades calculated proportionally.

10. Literary Gathering

Since the 20th year, the school has held a literary gathering once each semester. The Chinese language teachers in the school first propose a topic each in advance. One hour before the literary gathering, a temporary meeting is held to decide on the topic. The papers are graded by the Chinese language teachers, and five people are selected from each grade. Then, five more names are selected from the preliminary exam papers. So far, the interest has been very high.

Shanghai Peiming Girls' Middle School Tenth Anniversary Special Issue - Meritorious Women's Education 216

Peiming Girls' Middle School Tenth Anniversary Special Issue - Dedication and Harmony 217

Peiming Girls' Middle School Tenth Anniversary - Flourishing Talent 218

— Jiang

Principal Jin Yuezhang 219

(B) Moral Education 220

Middle school female students are in their youth, the golden age of life. At this time, their physical development is rapid, their reasoning increases, their emotions are stirred, their social impulses are strong, and their self-expression reaches its peak. It is imperative to pay attention to their natural interests and give them opportunities for balanced development, preventing dangerous tendencies. However, how to guide them according to circumstances, how to prevent problems before they arise, and how to correct them afterward are all difficult tasks. Therefore, moral education is the most challenging issue. The moral education at our school is the shared responsibility of a large number of faculty and staff, with the director of moral education overseeing it. Furthermore, we collaborate with students to cultivate "independent and self-governing students who build themselves."

(1) Standards of Moral Education—The school's training program focuses on the four aspects of moral, intellectual, physical, and social development, and also considers the needs of the times, setting six major goals aimed at promoting the inherent virtues of our nation: loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, trustworthiness, righteousness, and peace. These are listed below:

1. Vigorously abandon cowardice and complacency, and cultivate a spirit of courage and striving.

2. Vigorously abandon reliance and perfunctoriness, and cultivate the ability to be independent and responsible.

3. Vigorously abandon rashness and blind obedience, and cultivate careful and thorough thinking.

4. Vigorously abandon romantic extravagance, and cultivate habits of diligence and thrift.

5. Vigorously abandon hypocrisy and disunity, and cultivate a spirit of sincerity and solidarity.

6. Vigorously abandon selfishness and self-interest, and cultivate a concept of loving the country and loving the family.

(2) Examination of Conduct Grades

The examination of students' conduct grades is the responsibility of all faculty and staff members in addition to the moral education personnel. Based on the set goals, they observe students' daily activities at all times and in all places. Any factual manifestations in terms of personality, temperament, and behavior are recorded separately in the conduct examination book. At the end of the semester, these are compiled, assessed for merit, and reported to parents. If there are any instances of poor behavior or disciplinary violations, they are recorded in the conduct book and parents are notified immediately for mutual admonishment to improve the situation.

(3) Regulations for Rewards and Punishments

The school's various competitions, such as speeches and tests, emphasize group awards in order to inspire a spirit of cooperation and eliminate selfish notions. However, individual students who are ethical, studious, helpful, and diligent are still rewarded. The rewards are generally divided into certificates and scholarships. Students who have particularly good academic, conduct, and physical education performance after evaluation are given scholarships. In addition, certificates are given to those who pass all courses, have good conduct, and have no long-term absences.

Punishments are divided into admonishment, demerits, and expulsion. Students who commit violations or fail to work hard at their studies will be admonished to make them aware of their mistakes. A slightly more serious offense will result in a demerit as a warning. The most serious offenses will result in expulsion. The main items are as follows:

1. Those with bad character.

2. Those with unsound physical or mental health or suffering from infectious diseases.

3. Those who repeatedly fail to reform after being punished.

4. Those who evade semester exams.

5. Those who cheat on exams.

6. Those who insult teachers.

7. Those who seriously violate school rules.

8. Those whose improper behavior damages the school's reputation.

(4) Implementation of Moral Education—Based on the spirit of the Three Principles of the People and the principle of teacher-student cooperation, we aim to systematize thinking, discipline behavior, and cultivate students into sound citizens, with a focus on proactive guidance.

(A) The following aspects of the proactive approach are noteworthy:

1. Establish Class Tutors—The school's tutors are based on grade level, guiding the extracurricular activities and grade meetings of each grade level to develop self-governance abilities. They sometimes instill principles of conduct and self-cultivation to cultivate useful talents.

2. Establish Grade Meetings—The school drafts simple regulations for the organization of grade meetings. Under the guidance of the tutors, grade meetings are established for each grade level. Each grade meeting elects seven officers to be responsible for general affairs, academics, recreation, and physical education. Regular meetings are held every Monday afternoon after 4:00 PM to discuss ongoing matters, and inter-grade social gatherings are held in rotation each month to connect the students of each grade and provide entertainment.

3. Vigorously Implement Morning Exercises—The purpose of morning exercises is to exercise the body and cultivate the habit of waking up early. They are held every morning before breakfast. When students are on the field, in addition to being guided by physical education teachers, they are also monitored by moral education personnel and grade tutors for evaluation.

4. Conduct Individual and Group Talks—In order to foster harmonious relationships between teachers and students and to eliminate any distance between students and the school, it is essential to hold individual talks with students. When students' thoughts and behaviors are inappropriate, they are earnestly advised to correct them. Students who are suffering or have concerns can use the talks to express them. Individual talks are very effective. Group talks are often conducted by the principal, tutors, and moral education personnel, while school-wide talks are held during memorial weeks.

5. Publish Wall Newspapers—These wall newspapers are written entirely by students of each grade, thereby cultivating students' ability to express themselves. Each grade publishes them once every two weeks. The content is roughly divided into forums, current events, science, and literature. Particular emphasis is placed on academic exploration and the recording of current events. The results have been quite remarkable.

6. Hold Teacher-Student Gatherings—The school holds teacher-student social gatherings once or twice each semester. Students from each grade prepare programs, and teachers also act and participate in performances. Everyone enjoys themselves to the fullest and disperses happily. The next day, classes are still held as usual without any signs of fatigue, as the excitement greatly enhances their spirits.

7. Organize Thrift and National Salvation Groups—At a time when the economy is depleted and the nation is facing severe difficulties, students, as intellectuals, should practice frugality in clothing and food to fulfill their duty of loving the country. Therefore, thrift and national salvation groups have been established. The purpose is to ensure that all students practice not being extravagant, not decorating excessively, and not using foreign goods. The method is to publicly discuss and agree on regulations, which are implemented by the person in charge of the national groups, and to formulate reward and punishment measures. Students are generally able to comply. This spirit and action mark a new era for Shanghai girls' schools.

(B) Management Aspects

1. Strictly Prohibit Unauthorized Departure from School—The urban society is a breeding ground for all evils, and young people with weak wills are most prone to fall into depravity if they set foot in it. Therefore, management must be strict. The school conducts roll calls once or twice every night after boarding students return to their dormitories from self-study. Those who are found to have left without authorized leave are expelled immediately.

2. Inspect the Cleanliness of Dormitories and Classrooms—The cleanliness of dormitories and classrooms is not only related to the school's appearance but also to public health. In addition to regular major cleanings every week, the school also conducts daily cleanliness inspections. Statistics are compiled weekly, and the most outstanding results are awarded a cleanliness flag as encouragement.

3. Establish Leave Procedures—Taking leave is most likely to neglect studies. Students are not allowed to take leave unless they have illnesses or unavoidable circumstances. The leave procedures are divided into regular leave and class leave. Regular leave is for those who do not miss classes, and it is allowed once a week per person. Those who take leave to leave the school after classes on Saturday afternoons or on Sundays must return to school before 6:00 PM. If their families are in the local area, they must obtain a stay-out permit upon the formal request of their parents. For class leave, parents must send a letter to the moral education office stating the reason for the leave to be valid. In the case of sick leave, it must be certified by the school doctor to be approved.

(C) Future Plans

Anyone engaged in any work, if they want to achieve considerable results, how can they not work diligently and advance with the times? Only then will there be evidence of its fruit. All things are like this, how can education be an exception? Yue Zhang, who manages this school, has gone through six years. Although I have received advice from government officials, social elders, and school board members, I have fortunately avoided failure. However, at this tenth anniversary, it is important to be frugal and curb past shortcomings. We will formulate improvement plans in both material and spiritual aspects, in order to align with the direction of great governance.

A. Material Aspects

Constructing School Buildings: The school's buildings are rented, costing ten thousand yuan annually, which is not economical. Moreover, the impact on moral education and academic affairs is not insignificant. Yue Zhang has not forgotten this idea. In the past, the school board resolved to raise funds for construction. We have received letters from enthusiastic educators, stating that the fundraising has been somewhat successful. Once the funds are collected, we will purchase land and hire workers to start construction, obtaining permanent buildings so that the faculty can teach and students can study and play. This wish may be partially fulfilled.

(2) Increasing Equipment

1. Filling the Library: Students rely solely on textbooks to study at school. How much can they gain? Providing a library with a rich collection of books cannot be delayed. The school's old library has about nine thousand volumes, including classics, famous works in various subjects, and contemporary magazines. In the future, we plan to save on regular expenses and purchase two thousand books each semester to provide for the students.

2. Adding Laboratories: The importance of scientific experiments goes without saying. In the past, due to the insufficient school buildings, laboratories were still lacking. After the new school buildings are completed, we should first add a physics and chemistry laboratory and a botany and zoology laboratory for full research.

3. Equipment for Physical Education, Arts, and Business: For physical education, we plan to increase the equipment for the Boy Scouts and purchase sports equipment. The art department will establish a specialized classroom and purchase more models, etc. The number of business students is increasing daily, and the existing typewriters are insufficient. We must purchase more and set up a bank and consumer cooperative for their practice.

B. Spiritual Aspects

(1) Reforming Administrative Organization

1. Unifying Authority: School administration is a unified entity, divided into various departments. The relationship between them is very close. Their spirits are harmonious and inseparable, their duties are divided and have boundaries, and the result is that the administrative center is their common goal, and then the effect of command can be achieved. In the past, the school's organization sometimes lacked thorough consideration, which affected administrative efficiency. In the future, we will revise the regulations for administrative affairs, documents, academic affairs, moral education, and other departments, so as to achieve the effect of unifying authority.

2. Communicating the Spirit of Moral Education: In recent schools, moral education and teaching have been separate, and those in charge have become accustomed to viewing moral education and teaching as two separate things. Those being taught also divide character and learning into two separate things. Cultivating in this way is difficult to achieve good results. School authorities examine past mistakes, and there is the implementation of the unification of moral education. We combine the two departments of academic affairs and moral education and place one director of guidance. The school has also tried this system, and the past mistakes, it is said, have not been remedied. However, adding the responsibilities of the entire school's moral education to one person, considering this and that, how much energy is there? Yue Zhang believes that the unification of moral education is not in the nominal correction, but in the integration of the spirit and methods in implementation. If we constantly think of moral education as teaching and teaching as moral education, we can avoid the hard work of affairs and gain the meaning of the unification of moral education. My humble opinion is to ask for wisdom.

3. Common Life: The lifestyle habits of faculty and staff are models for students in everything, which is called setting a good example. If they are not careful about diet and living, students will be influenced invisibly and reduce the effectiveness of education a lot. It is recorded, "The one who starts driving a horse, reverses it, the cart is in front of the horse," is this what it means? In the near future, teachers and students will practice a common life, and all aspects of clothing, diet, and recreation will be simple and plain with students.

4. Adding Classes: The school is divided into three departments: elementary school, junior high school, and senior high school. The senior high school is divided into general studies, business studies, and teacher training (now ordered to end), a total of thirteen classes. This winter vacation, the junior high school and senior high school will add one freshman class each, and the elementary school will add a kindergarten to expand.

(2) Implementing Career Guidance

1. Set up a Career Guidance Department: In addition to the administrative, academic, and moral education departments, we will add a career guidance department to provide organized and systematic guidance.

2. Specially Set Up Career Lectures: We will hire career education experts to give lectures at the school every week, so that students can acquire advanced knowledge of careers and the path to engaging in careers.

3. Career Introduction: We will earnestly contact the business community so that the school can do its best to introduce students after graduation.

(3) Expanding the School's Educational Functions

1. Connecting Families: Families and schools are closely related. The school must clearly understand students' living habits at home and the family environment. The family should also know the students' life situation at school. In this way, the school has a guideline for the individual training of students, and what the family expects from the school is also easy to handle. Moreover, as parents have more opportunities to contact teachers, the relationship becomes more and more cordial. Intercommunication has an invisible effect on education that is not small.

2. Communicating with Society: "Closing the door to build a car, going out the door may not fit the track," educators also say "school is society" and "education is life." Based on the above, schools and society should strive to communicate in order to become one.

3. Holding Civil Schools: School education and social education have the responsibility to depend on each other and help each other. Within the possible range of schools, such as people's schools, reading newspapers, and writing on behalf of others, should be attached to make up for the deficiencies of social education. The school plans to run an attached civil school in each semester to reduce social illiteracy. All aspects of the school need to be improved at all times. The above is just a general overview. The advancement of any career, the economy is its driving force. In the future, Yue Zhang will see how the school's financial resources are, and weigh the urgency of the matter, seek truth from facts, and strive for gradual perfection, so that students can improve both physically and mentally. As for personal talent, I know that I am inadequate, and I hope that there are outstanding people who can teach me.
