Telecommunications Special Issue

Answering Questions About the Three-Minute System 238

— Zhen

It is noted that long-distance telephone calls in various European and American countries are all based on a three-minute system. The Ministry of Communications-operated long-distance telephone services in various provinces also adopt the three-minute system as a principle, with some using a five-minute system during the initial establishment period. In December of last year, price standards for three-minute and five-minute systems were stipulated based on actual distances to standardize them. Currently, domestic long-distance telephone equipment has reached a considerable level of development, and international wireless telephone services are scheduled to be implemented. In order to meet international call standards and facilitate future international calls, the Ministry of Communications has decided to adopt the three-minute system nationwide, starting from April, according to spatial distance as the standard. This is the reason for the Ministry of Communications' revision of long-distance telephone prices.

Unexpectedly, some users on the Beijing-Shanghai line have expressed dissatisfaction after the implementation of these prices. My friend Mr. Wu wrote to me, raising three points for discussion regarding this matter: (1) Each call between the two locations is not clear, and repeated explanations are needed. Due to dialect differences, it is practically impossible to complete the call within three minutes. (2) In the past, a five-minute call between Beijing and Shanghai cost one unit at $1.50. Now, a four-minute call costs $2.40, an increase of 60%! (3) According to the government's decree, for any monopolistic or franchised enterprise, whether government-run, commercially-run, or jointly-run, if it intends to increase the burden on the people due to excessive expenses, it must first have the principles determined by the Central Political Conference and then submitted to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation, unless otherwise stipulated by law; otherwise, it is considered illegal. You are familiar with the transportation industry, so can you enlighten me on this matter? Mr. Wu's words have some merit. Upon further study, the following questions arise: (1) Is three minutes sufficient for a call? (2) Does the three-minute system increase the price by 60%? (3) Is the Ministry of Communications' revision of long-distance call prices illegal?

To facilitate communication for the public, the Ministry of Communications has revised various telegram fees, resulting in an annual loss of about $500,000. Furthermore, the express call fee for long-distance calls, which was originally three times the regular fee, was reduced to two times the regular fee in October of last year, resulting in an annual loss of over $100,000. These facts are evident and visible to all. To say that this revision of long-distance call prices is intentionally increasing the burden on the public is hardly fair. After the author obtained the truth, I responded to the questions as follows:

(1) Three Minutes is Sufficient for a Call: The so-called three-minute system is defined as three minutes from the time the receiver answers the call to the time they indicate the end of the call. Within this time limit is the first call, and beyond this is the second call. Continuous calls must not exceed two calls. According to experts, those who use long-distance telephones are usually dealing with urgent and simple matters that can be resolved with a few words. Three minutes is sufficient and there is no need to ramble on and require five minutes. If a matter cannot be resolved within three minutes, one can use the telephone telegram service instead of relying on long-distance calls. As for the issue of unclear sound quality, it is a technical problem and has nothing to do with time. Even if the competent authority stipulates a call time of ten minutes, it will be useless. After all, one can communicate as if face-to-face even across vast oceans. How can it be that communication between Beijing and Shanghai, which are so close, cannot flow smoothly?

(2) Call Prices Have Not Increased by 60%: To make the comparison clearer, I have transcribed the two sets of standard prices issued by the Ministry of Communications as follows:

Three-Minute System

Distance in Kilometers (Spatial Distance) Price (Silver Dollars)

0-20 0.10

20-40 0.20

40-60 0.30

60-80 0.40

80-100 0.50

100-125 0.60

125-150 0.70

150-175 0.80

175-200 0.90

200-225 1.00

225-250 1.10

250-275 1.20

275-300 1.30

Five-Minute System

Distance in Kilometers (Spatial Distance) Price (Silver Dollars)

0-15 0.10

15-30 0.20

30-45 0.30

45-60 0.40

60-75 0.50

75-90 0.60

90-110 0.70

110-130 0.80

130-150 0.90

150-170 1.00

170-190 1.10

190-210 1.20

210-230 1.30

Looking at the above table, in terms of the minimum distance, the three-minute system is for 20 kilometers, which is 5 kilometers more than the 15 kilometers for the five-minute system. In terms of the same call cost, with a fee of $1.30, the three-minute system can cover 300 kilometers, while the five-minute system can only cover 230 kilometers. The spatial distance between Beijing and Shanghai is about 270 kilometers, so the stipulated price is $1.20, which is $0.30 less than the original five-minute system. If we consider two calls totaling six minutes, the three-minute system charges $2.40, while the five-minute system charges $3.00. For the same six minutes, the three-minute system is actually 20% cheaper. Furthermore, there is a difference between spatial distance and line distance. The line has many bends due to engineering reasons, while spatial distance forms a straight line between the two points. Compared to each other, the difference is about 20%. In the past, distance was calculated based on the line, but now it is based on spatial standards. This loss is another 20%!

In terms of the price on the Beijing-Shanghai line, the original price was based on a three-minute calculation when the Beijing government first opened the Shanghai telephone exchange. Later, the call time was temporarily changed to five minutes for one call, but the price was not increased. Later, as the line extended to various places, call prices were still calculated according to the previously determined ratio, resulting in lower call prices on the Beijing-Shanghai line compared to other lines nationwide. Now, the Ministry of Communications has reduced the original three-minute system price—$1.50—to the current price—$1.20—for fees. There seems to be nothing wrong with this for the convenience of public communication.

It is noted that long-distance calls between Beijing and Tianjin are based on a three-minute system, which has been in effect for years. The distance between Beijing and Tianjin is 112 kilometers, and the price is set at $0.60, which is convenient for the public. It is also noted that the five-minute system for long-distance telephones in various parts of the country has been gradually changed to the three-minute system since April 1st of this year, and no objections have been heard. Now, the distance between Beijing and Shanghai is 270 kilometers, and the three-minute system is implemented, with a reduced price of $1.20. What difficulties do users still feel?

(3) Is the Ministry of Communications' Revision of Telephone Prices Illegal? I am not a legal expert and therefore cannot answer this question. However, I have heard that the Ministry of Communications' revisions to telegram and telephone prices over the years, revisions to postal and shipping prices, and the Ministry of Railways' revisions to transportation prices on various routes do not seem to have been reviewed by the Legislative Yuan. People in society have also not considered them illegal. Should the transportation services operated by the Ministry of Communications be compared with ordinary government-run enterprises? Is there already a legal basis for the Ministry of Communications' revision of telegram and telephone prices? If you ask the transportation authorities, I believe they will have a clear answer.

In summary, the Ministry of Communications' current regulations on long-distance telephone prices are aimed at adopting the current international system for communication with international individuals and taking into account the national economic situation to cooperate with individuals in society. It is definitely not comparable to those who disregard the interests of the people for the purpose of profit. At the same time, if users have any opinions, the Ministry of Communications will sincerely communicate with them and accept them as much as possible within the scope of possibility. You are a leader and are admired by all. I hope you can provide more guidance to dispel the confusion of the general public. Thank you very much.

Mr. Wu heard this and said: "Good! Write 'Answering Questions About the Three-Minute System'."

The Benefits of Installing a Telephone 239

— Zhong Ming

In the previous issue of this publication, the article "Comparison of Telegraph and Long-Distance Telephone" written by Mr. Qinghua provided an extremely detailed analysis of the benefits of telegrams and telephones, giving the public a very clear understanding of the differences between long-distance telephones and telegrams. This allows people to determine when it is appropriate to make a phone call or send a telegram. However, what Mr. Qinghua presented was only a comparison of the benefits of telegrams and telephones, and not simply a lecture on the efficacy of telegrams or telephones. This publication has repeatedly recorded the efficacy of telegrams, and it can be said that it has been fully elaborated. As for telephones, there has been little clear description.

When it comes to the efficacy of telephones, it can be said to be an inexhaustible subject, difficult to express in a single sentence. To describe the efficacy of telephones, I think it is best to use the sentence that Jiufu Company used to describe its own medicine called "Bailingji", which is "Unexpected efficacy!" These eight characters are really true. The various effects of telephones, when talked about, are indeed superficial, but ordinary people often neglect them because they are superficial, resulting in many indirect or direct losses of benefits and opportunities, or needlessly spending a lot of energy, time and money!

Having said that, I might as well give a simple example: Last summer, the weather was extremely hot, and the indoor temperature was often around ninety-seven or eighty degrees, sometimes even exceeding one hundred degrees. Therefore, ice shops were everywhere in the capital city. As usual, in such hot weather, doing such a timely business should have been thriving. However, the fact was not so, because there were too many ice shops, and the supply exceeded the demand, so there was not much profit to be made. However, a few of them did do some business. They did not rely solely on retail sales, but their main transactions were in the delivery of whole buckets of ice cream. It turned out that these few had foresight and were different from the others, and they all had telephones installed in their stores. Many people in government offices, public residences, and shops wanted to drink ice to relieve the heat when they were busy with work and sweating like rain. If they asked servants or went to buy it themselves, it would be uneconomical in terms of time, and who would be willing to run under the scorching sun? So they all chose these few shops with telephones to call for delivery. When the ice shops received a call, they immediately sent someone to ride a bicycle with ice cream and rush over, arriving in a moment. How satisfied the customers were! No wonder the business was thriving!

The above example has shown the efficacy of telephones clearly. Ice shops gained a lot of business because they had telephones installed, which is a benefit; because they had telephones installed, people could find them or they could attract people's love, which is an opportunity; as for telephone users, they can leisurely lie on the sofa, lightly dial the phone, and order ice cream to drink, which saves money, time and energy, and is also so comfortable. The principle of this example can be extended to all kinds of businesses, and is applicable to anyone. In other words, telephones have the efficacy of helping all undertakings to develop.

However, the efficacy of telephones is not limited to this. They also have the efficacy of providing quick access to news, familiarity with market conditions, assisting public security, enhancing friendship, breaking loneliness, and rescuing emergencies. Whether you are in business or politics, you must have quick access to news. If you have a telephone, news will be easily transmitted, either reporting to others or inquiring from others. As for people in business, in particular, they need to be familiar with market conditions in order to buy and sell. If they do not use the telephone and rely on running around on their own feet, it will not only be laborious and time-consuming, but also the market conditions they obtain will be limited. Speaking of assisting public security, telephones can especially exert great efficacy. For example, if a fire or robbery occurs somewhere, you can use the power of the telephone to immediately notify the news to the fire prevention agency to arrive at the scene to rescue and reduce the damage, or the public security agency to send police to arrest the bandits. Also, if one or two close friends are in the south or north of the city, and they have been separated for a long time and miss each other, but personally visiting each other is too far and time-consuming, and they are especially afraid of not being able to meet, at this time they can chat with him on the phone and express their feelings, or make an appointment to meet in person. The telephone should be given the first credit for enhancing the friendship between the two parties. Also, when we are bored, we can also use the telephone to find a friend to talk to, thereby breaking the loneliness and giving comfort. As for emergencies such as sudden acute illnesses or a pregnant woman giving birth in the middle of the night, the telephone is the most precious thing for people. The efficacy of telephones is endless and unimaginable. It is most appropriate to describe it with the four words "Unexpected!".

There is one more thing I would like to talk to you about here. The telephone bureaus in Shanghai, Tianjin, Beiping, Wuhan, Qingdao, the Capital, Wuxian, Zhenjiang, Yantai, etc., which are under the Ministry of Communications, all have inquiry desks, which not only answer public inquiries about telephone numbers, but also answer user inquiries about various local affairs, free of charge. This scope includes: (1) Standard time; (2) Location of the fire that occurred on the day; (3) Daily business hours of post offices and telegraph offices; (4) Locations and prices of domestic and international telegrams; (5) Locations and postage rates for domestic and international mail; (6) Daily programs and times of various entertainment venues; (7) Departure times and prices of trains, ships, and long-distance buses; (8) Telephone rental fees in the city and locations and prices of long-distance telephone calls. This measure has been implemented since April 1 this year and has been highly praised by the public. Therefore, telephone users in major ports, in addition to enjoying various benefits, are in effect hiring a loyal personnel consultant.

Amplified Loudspeaker 240

— Long Sheng

The Shanghai Telegraph Bureau's Contribution to the National Games 241

— Bao Zhen

Establishing a temporary telegraph office to send and receive telegrams and sell telephones

The National Games is a very important event for the future of sports in our country and can attract the attention of the entire nation. Previous events held in Hangzhou, Nanjing, and other places were all extremely grand. In order to promote sports and facilitate news, the Ministry of Communications has repeatedly ordered the postal administrations and telegraph offices in Hangzhou, Nanjing, and other places to set up temporary postal and telegraph offices at the venues during the Games, which have been very successful and have won high praise from the society. The 6th National Games will open in Shanghai on National Day this year. At that time, there will be a grand scene of bustling traffic on the roads in the city center. It is reported that the Ministry of Communications has already ordered the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau to follow the precedent and set up a temporary telegraph office in the city center venue, which will open at the same time as the Games.

The main task of the temporary telegraph office is to transmit telegrams reporting the results of the Games. In order to ensure rapid transmission, Webster telegraph machines or Creed telegraph machines will be installed in the temporary telegraph office. On the one hand, efforts will be made to free up telegraph lines to prepare for opening direct connections to various places, so that some of the telegrams sent from the temporary telegraph office do not have to be scanned and transferred through the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau, in order to be fast. On the other hand, the Games will be specially allowed to send hard news telegrams reporting the results of the Games on account, so that the Games can send news of the Games to newspapers in various places at any time, so that the people in other places who cannot attend the Games can also learn about the results of the Games in the newspaper the next day. At the same time, the temporary telegraph office is equipped with public telephones and sells local and long-distance telephones to facilitate communication. It can be seen that the establishment of the temporary telegraph office is entirely to support the Games in transmitting news of the Games and is by no means for profit.

When the last National Games was held in Beijing, in order to give preferential treatment to athletes from various provinces and cities in sending telegrams, the Ministry of Communications specially formulated a preferential treatment method for athletes from the National Games to send telegrams, which was printed together with the domestic social telegram rules and distributed to the athletes at the Games. This year's Games is the same. The Ministry of Communications has ordered the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau to follow the above-mentioned preferential treatment method for athletes to send telegrams. According to the provisions of the method, the Chinese and English coded telegrams sent by the athletes themselves reporting their whereabouts, daily life, and sports news can be paid according to the price of domestic social telegrams (ie, 2 cents per Chinese character and 4 cents per English character), but they are still listed as ordinary telegrams for transmission and are delivered as soon as they arrive (according to the regulations, social telegrams that arrive at the receiving telegraph office after 9 pm on the day and before 8 am the next morning should be delivered after 8 am the next day. However, the reduced-price telegrams sent by athletes are still delivered as soon as they arrive according to the ordinary telegram rules), which can be said to be a special treatment. The male and female athletes of the Games have come from afar from various provinces and cities. Although they are only separated from their parents, brothers, and sisters in their hometowns, they cannot help but miss them. Now that there is an opportunity to send telegrams at a low price, they can send telegrams to comfort them at any time. Thousands of miles away, it is like talking in the same room. The athletes can relieve their worries, work hard in sports, and win the championship.

In addition, the scope of the text of domestic social telegrams has been expanded. Telegrams celebrating "victory" can also be sent as social telegrams. If the family members or relatives and friends of the athletes receive a telegram informing them of the victory in a certain sport, or learn of the victory from the newspaper, they can send social telegrams to express their congratulations and encourage them. After receiving congratulatory telegrams, the athletes will inevitably be more excited, and therefore the competition results will break the national record.

In order to implement the policy of joint postal and telegraph services, the Ministry of Communications has ordered the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau to consult with the Shanghai Postal Administration to set up a temporary post office and telegraph office in the same place, in order to set an example for joint postal and telegraph services and facilitate public communication. Now that the opening of the Games is not far away, the above-mentioned temporary joint postal and telegraph office will soon meet the public.

Shanghai Telegraph Bureau's Review of the Purchase of the Qianliangmiao Base 242

— Hua

The Shanghai Telegraph Bureau recently purchased 300 mu of land at Qianliangmiao Station on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway, south of Beichangqiao Town, in order to expand its transmitting radio station. The Ministry of Interior announced the purchase, which caused misunderstandings among some local people, who repeatedly appealed to the Yuan and Ministry to withdraw the order. Various newspapers have also repeatedly reported on this. This article reports that the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau's purchase of the base this time is of great importance to the development of telecommunications and transportation. In order to dispel the doubts of people in the society, the true situation of the process is recorded as follows:

Shanghai is a world commercial port and the hub of our country's foreign trade. Therefore, telegraph communication is extremely busy. Since the invention of short-wave radio, due to business and technical reasons, it has become the center of the domestic radio communication network. In the 20th year of the Republic of China, the former Shanghai Radio General Station was unable to cope with the busy business and the original manual transceivers. It had long planned to improve the equipment to facilitate communication, but at that time, the transmitting radio station was cramped in the Shangdeng Middle School in Lujiabang and could not be expanded. Moreover, since the school building was repeatedly discussed for relocation, radio communication was in danger of being interrupted from time to time. Therefore, for the sake of permanent solution, it was approved by the Ministry of Communications to purchase 200 mu of land in Qianliangmiao for the construction of a transmitting station. At that time, the Ministry of Interior also issued a public announcement, and it was not heard that the local people had any opposition. Until the January 28 Incident occurred, the purchase was temporarily shelved, and the transmitting station was temporarily moved to three places: Maigen Road and Xinzha Road on Zhonghua Road to barely cope. However, each of these places was narrow and the antenna could not be expanded. Moreover, the surrounding tall buildings were towering and the radio waves were often blocked. The communication efficiency was inevitably affected. Since the merger of the bureaus last year, the telegraph business has become even more heavy, and the expansion of radio equipment is even more urgent. Therefore, the old proposal was followed and land was purchased in Qianliangmiao for construction.

This time, the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau purchased 300 mu of land in Qianliangmiao, which is 100 mu more than in the 20th year of the Republic of China. The reason for this is the change in the plan and also the technical needs. In order to avoid mutual feelings between the antennas, there must be sufficient distance between each payment. Approximately, each directional antenna Bodhi tree requires 6 mu of land, and non-directional antenna requires 3 mu. In addition, there are two wavelengths for day and night work, and two antennas must be prepared for each. Therefore, the planned antennas are 58 pairs, which require approximately 230 mu of land. In addition, the construction of houses and walkways and the reserved expansion space, etc., must be 50 or 60 mu. Therefore, the area of the new transmitting station base in Shanghai must be at least 300 mu, which is not an excessive requirement.

According to radio communication, it all depends on the transmission of radio waves, and the quality of the transmission of radio waves depends entirely on whether there are tall buildings or forests around the transmitting radio station that obstruct the range. The area north of Qianliangmiao Station is empty and boundless, which is very suitable for the above-mentioned conditions. Therefore, it is very suitable as a radio transmitting station base. Moreover, it is only about 4 kilometers away from the high-voltage transmission line laid along the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway by the Huashang Electric Company in the South City. In the future, the expansion and connection will be quite convenient for the power supply. Therefore, this place was specially selected for application. In fact, the place does have various objective conditions and is not a deliberate demand for a certain place.

In summary, the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau's purchase of the Qianliangmiao base is a necessary move for the development of telecommunications and transportation, and there is no intention to seek profit in the area. We sincerely hope that the local people understand the importance of state-owned enterprises and will not make persistent criticisms. We especially hope that the media will provide unified support, in order to dispel the unnecessary misunderstandings of the social scholars, which is our hope.

A Brief Account of the Newly Revised Domestic Telegraph Business Regulations (Continued from the previous issue) 243

— Bao Zhen

(4) Regarding the methods for delivering telegrams: Delivering telegrams is one of the important tasks of the telegraph office. Therefore, the telegraph office must have detailed and comprehensive regulations for delivering incoming telegrams in order to increase the speed of delivery. In view of this, the Ministry of Communications has specifically stipulated in detail the methods for delivering telegrams and the price of special effort fees in the newly revised domestic telegraph business regulations, so that each telegraph office has something to follow. The improvements compared with the old regulations are briefly listed as follows: 1. When a messenger delivers a telegram and encounters that the recipient's residence is closed or no one is willing to receive it on his behalf, he should try to leave a notice at the place and return the telegram to the office, waiting for the recipient or his representative to bring the seal to the office to collect it. If this telegram waiting to be collected is not collected after 12 hours, it should be sent again. If it is still impossible to deliver it properly, it should be handled according to the method for undeliverable telegrams and a notice should be published in the newspaper to solicit collection. (2) Telegrams sent to passengers on ships arriving at the port should be sent before the recipient disembarks as far as possible. If time does not permit, the telegrams may be sent to the manager of the ship. (3) Ordinary, urgent, or social Chinese coded telegrams should be translated into text by the telegraph office before delivery, and no translation fee will be charged. The above three rules are quite convenient for the recipients and are not the beginning of the improvement of the service spirit of the telegraph office.

As for the price of the special effort fee, it has been slightly increased compared with the old regulations in order to meet actual needs. However, after the price of the special effort fee has been increased, the Ministry of Communications has strictly ordered each telegraph office to strictly abide by the stipulated prices when charging fees in the future, and there must be no more cases of deliberately violating the order and arbitrarily raising prices and demanding. If the recipient encounters a messenger who extorts fees, he can detail the facts and evidence and appeal directly to the Telegraph Administration of the Ministry of Communications for strict punishment in accordance with the regulations.

How to Calculate the Number of Words in English Plain Language? 244

— Wei Li

—Please pay attention to the senders—

The Shanghai Telegraph Bureau, the International Radio Station, and the Sanshui Line Telegraph Receiving and Sending Office under the International Telecommunications Bureau, in view of the fact that there is no definite standard for calculating the number of words in English telegrams, have specially drafted a "Provisional Method for Calculating the Number of Words in English Plain Language Telegrams." Now, for the convenience of the senders, it is translated into Chinese in summary and introduced here:

Provisional Method for Calculating the Number of Words in English Plain Language Telegrams

A, Words in the dictionary: (No more than fifteen letters are charged as one word)

(1) Compound words that are continuously connected with a hyphen can be counted as one word by removing the hyphen.

(2) Contractions of negative words are counted as one word, removing the apostrophe.

Example Don’t can be written as Dont and counted as one word

B, Words not in the dictionary

(3) Auxiliary verbs that are combined with the word not to form a contraction are counted as one word.

Example Must Not can be written as Mustont and counted as one word.

(4) Prefixes un added to a word and connected to form a word are counted as a single word according to common usage.

(See Webster's New International Dictionary, 1935 Edition, page 2757. New International Dictonary 1935 Edjtin Page 2757)

Prefixes Yester used to indicate time and added to other words to form a word are counted as one word.

Example Yestermonth (counted as one word)

(6) Cardinal numbers combined with a noun to form an adjective can be counted as one word.

Example 1. Sixcylinder car (counted as two words) But Sixcylinders (counted as two words)

Example 2. Fivedollar note (counted as two words) But Fivedollars (counted as two words)

(7) Artificial words that are invented with the intention of reducing telegraph fees must be counted separately according to the words.

Example Relet=Refer (to your) letter (counted as two words)

Relet=Refer (to your) telegram (counted as two words)

(8) The names of publications, pictures, films, companies, foreign firms, societies, organizations, etc., must be counted separately according to the words.

Example 1. Telegraphy and telephony (counted as three words)

2. Bank of Communications (counted as three words)

3. Four devils (counted as two words)

4. Young menschristianassociation (counted as four words)

(9) The initials of a group representing the names of famous groups and organizations are counted as follows:

(1) In the address (used as an abbreviated address) is counted as one word. For example, NCDN Shanghai. However, the sender is responsible for the responsibility if the delivery is unsuccessful or there is no delivery.

(2) In the text can be counted as one word: for example, DKK, JCJL, NCDN. (To be continued)

Reply to Mr. Xu Kang of the Capital Police Department 245

— Reporter

I have received your letter inquiring about the receipt and sending of telegrams, and I reply as follows:

(1) For telegrams sent to Japan, if the text is in Chinese four-code, the name and address of the recipient can be translated into Japanese to facilitate delivery.

(2) Japanese telegrams (spelled with kana) sent to Japan can be received and sent by the International Radio Station, as well as the Qingdao, Sifang, and Cangkou telegraph offices.

(3) Only Arabic numerals can be mixed in Japanese telegrams, and each numeral is counted as a Japanese letter.

(4) Only accented letters are allowed in Western telegrams, and the rest are not allowed. Also, chji should be calculated as two letters.

(5) There are no restrictions on the text allowed for code words and cipher words. Any word composed of 26 letters can be called a code word or cipher word. Arabic numerals can also be mixed in code word or cipher word telegrams, but the number of words cannot exceed half of the total number of words in the telegram.

(6) Code words are composed of invented words (containing five letters), or use real words but do not contain the original meaning of the words, or are composed of a mixture of real words and invented words. For example: Klvgk Cramn is composed entirely of invented words, and Klvgk Batci Continental hotel is composed of a mixture of invented words and plain language words and are regarded as code word telegrams.

Any word or combination of letters that does not conform to the regulations for plain language and code words, such as the word Cramgliork, is an invented word that does not conform to the regulations for code words (because it contains more than five letters), so it should be regarded as a cipher word.

A Gift 246

— Jiu

One clear autumn evening, clear mercury-like moonlight painted a layer of beautiful silver-gray on the four French windows near the balcony. The chilly September breeze playfully gently blew the violet-colored long window curtains. The incandescent electric light, passing through the light green lampshade, appeared bright and complemented the milky white walls, the color tone was very harmonious. Johnson sat comfortably on the sofa with the day's newspaper, Mary, quietly sat in the chair, earnestly knitting a woolen shirt, the room was shrouded in a quiet, happy, and harmonious atmosphere.

Suddenly, Johnson shouted as if he had discovered some miracle, "Mary! Come and see! There is good news here! Our problem can be solved."

Mary, who was earnestly knitting a woolen shirt, was startled by his sudden shout, and put down the woolen shirt and walked gracefully to Johnson's side, and scolded coquettishly, "What miracle did you discover! Is it worth shouting like that?"

Johnson said with a smile, "My love, don't be angry, come, please come and sit here, I have good things to show you!" As he said, he dragged Mary over and sat side by side on the sofa.

"Mary! Look, isn't this good news? Anna and Paxun are going to attend the 6th National Games? I can't think of the most agile and freshest way to encourage them to work hard and cheer them on, and celebrate their final victory. Now it's good, social telegrams can solve this problem."

"Yes! How good is that!" Mary looked at the newspaper and said with a smile, "It's really better than any gift. Because it's so meaningful!"

"Then let's send it tomorrow!" Johnson thought for a while and said, "And that day is October 10th, we can celebrate their victory on the one hand, and celebrate our National Day on the other hand, which is killing two birds with one stone!"

Johnson is right, social telegrams are a very good gift.

Fundraising to Establish a Bedbug Extermination Company 247

— Chui

According to news from Xin Sheng Society yesterday, several experts engaged in entomological research are currently discussing the organization of a bedbug extermination company. It is said that bedbugs are a common and special pest in the insect species, living by sucking human blood, and their reproduction is so fast that no one can cure them. They are of a global nature. Currently, all major cities in the world have traces of this pest. The British and Americans call them pests, and also call them Nanjing bugs. In fact, this bug is not produced in China. The poor and remote areas of China where transportation is inconvenient have no such bugs at all, which is clear evidence. Nanjing has gained the notoriety of this bedbug, which is really the misfortune of Nanjing and the great fortune of the bedbug.

It is said that the name Nanjing bug is based on a Japanese term. Japan named it after the fact that bedbugs are particularly numerous in Nanjing, China, but this is actually a mistake. The name of the bedbug as Nanjing originally came from the Treaty of Nanjing. Since the signing of the treaty, in the past hundred years, most of the people's fat and oil in our country have been absorbed by foreigners, so that our country is burned in the skin and bones, and the appearance is withered, the people are poor and the wealth is exhausted, and the Luo excavated are exhausted, mostly affected by the Treaty of Nanjing. Therefore, the political bedbugs are more harmful than the insect bedbugs. Therefore, the name of the bedbug is Nanjing, and it is quite appropriate to be worthy of its name.

According to the research of entomologists, bedbugs are a common and special pest in the insect species, living by sucking human blood, and their reproduction is so fast that no one can cure them. It is true that wherever bedbugs go, people have no day of peace. If there are bedbugs in the house, they cannot sleep well, their spirits are tired, they cannot catch them all, they cannot search them all, they are prevented in one place and born in another, they are removed on the left and disturbed on the right. Therefore, the invasion of bedbugs is no different from political aggression. Therefore, the name of the bedbug is Nanjing, which has a profound meaning, although the facts are different, but the nature is the same.

However, the disturbance of bedbugs to public security has a certain period. In spring and summer, the clowns jump on the beams and are rampant. In autumn and winter, they slightly converge and hide in the depths, not daring to come out to make trouble again. And the chaos bugs in politics have no fixed time and no fixed direction, taking advantage of people's dangers and strangling people's emergencies, and there is no way to punish them. Therefore, it is easy to remove insect bedbugs, but it is difficult to remove political bedbugs, and there are many kinds of bedbugs, not only Nanjing bugs. Others, such as local tyrants and evil gentry who bully the people, are also bedbugs. Corrupt officials who exploit the common people are also bedbugs. Others, such as treacherous merchants, are all bedbugs. There are so many bedbugs, even if a special company is set up, I am afraid that they cannot be caught all.

Qingyun Ancient Temple 248

— Hua Jia

It was on just such an early autumn day, in the distant south where the morning still held the warmth of summer heat, that we two young men were hurrying along. The path from the lower temple to the upper temple was a rugged mountain road of nearly an hour's distance. However, if we didn't ascend the mountain in this early morning, before the sun exerted its power, I believe we would be like the birds in the fairy tale about the southern sun country, who, greedy for human flesh, forgot that the sun would rise and scorch them to death. Indeed, if one were to travel this hour-long mountain path during the fiercest heat of the sun, it would surely make one more susceptible to catching a cold, which would be precisely the opposite of the purpose of climbing the mountain. Originally, on the way up the mountain, there was a means of transportation called "shan dou" (mountain sedan), which was often used, and if you simply informed the receptionist monk at the lower temple, he would quickly summon it for you, as the people who carried the shan dou were the "xiang huo" (a type of worker who did menial labor in the temple) of his immortal temple. However, because we were both young men, and both had boasted of our ability to walk vigorously, we resolved to forego all means of transportation and tackle this journey, which was not short.

When I had visited this place several years ago, the path up the mountain was still the bird path used by woodcutters to chop firewood, but now it was different. The winds of the city had destroyed the wilderness, replaced by a flat highway. Although the flatness salvaged the rugged and difficult mountain road, it could not withstand the heat of the sun; on the contrary, walking on these flat highways only made the heat more unbearable. When the flat road was behind us, we had already reached the mountainside. On the mountainside, we still had to walk the winding paths called "sheep intestines," but it was much cooler. The mountain was full of tall cedar and palm trees, providing shade that made the breeze on the road extremely pleasant. It was like walking on the road to paradise, forgetting fatigue and walking happily.

Beside the road was a small stream, mountain water cascading down from the waterfall, so its clear, cool, and pleasant atmosphere, and the murmuring sound of the flowing water, immersed the entire valley in a joyful melody. The singing of birds in the early morning was particularly melodious and clear, combined with the unknown mountain songs sung by the wood-gathering women, honestly, it would be enchanting to be captivated in this valley. However, because our stomachs felt hungry, poetic emotions could no longer detain us, and we continued to advance.

"Qingyun Ancient Temple"

A burst of murmuring chanting of Buddha's name wafted into our ears, and we also discovered a horizontal inscribed board with these words on a large fire-resistant wall. Thus, our destination had arrived. Moreover, in my experience, it was possible here to obtain a vegetarian meal that wasn't too bad to fill our hungry stomachs. Therefore, we quickly went to the reception hall to find the receptionist monk. Alas, what a letdown! When we met, the result was a disappointment beyond my expectations. Perhaps because his snobbish eyes had discerned from the embellishments of our clothing that we were not the "benefactors" he had envisioned, the ensuing reception was a cold one. A few minutes later, he sent a young novice to take us to tour the scenic spots of their ancient temple. Thus, following the cries of "Amitabha," we walked past places like the Immortals' Cauldron, Sleeping Buddha Pavilion, Money-Shaking Tree, Guanyin Hall, Great Hero Hall, Eighteen Arhats, and so on, and then returned to the reception hall. By this time, our stomachs were forcing us to negotiate with the receptionist monk regardless of everything. In the end, we used a symbol and badge of "officialdom" to divert his snobbish gaze and obtained a not very cold vegetarian meal to satisfy our hunger. In retaliation, we were also stingy with our generosity, and after eating, we left without saying a word.

On our way back, we discussed how the ancient temple, although hidden deep in the mountains, was still immersed in the dream of gilding gold.

Abandoned Child 249

— Zhen

Under a withered, moldy electric lamp, the same color as an old woman's face, a child, not yet two years old, whose parents were unknown, gradually went from convulsions into a dying state, and departed this cruel world.

Two lines of glistening tears hung under the old woman's eyelids. After a year of personally caring for him, she was as attached to him as if he were her own child, grieving. Just a quarter of an hour ago, the child had called out "Mama," and that sound still remained crisply in her ears. Tomorrow, tomorrow, even this corpse would be eternally lost from her hands! She bowed her head, as if in repentance:

"Child, my calling you that is perhaps an insult to you! But you can't blame me, you know, your parents haven't sent any news for a long time, and not a penny of money, it's been four months! And I can't find them."

She leaned against the edge of the bed, staring blankly at the child, crying sadly.

Although she was innocent in her conscience toward him, her heart couldn't withstand this accidental pressure. In a daze, she felt that she was still the perpetrator of this tragedy. This little soul wouldn't forgive her in the underworld. When he was sick, she hadn't let him see a doctor. When he was hungry, her milk wasn't enough, she hadn't fed him his fill. Now that he was dead, this was the last time he troubled her, and she still couldn't give him a small coffin to atone for her sins... An inexplicable terror was surrounding her, on the bed, in the corners of the room: she was like being thrown into a frigid, snowy area, her body just trembling, her two hands with protruding veins touching the withered cheeks of the child.

"You can't go with him. It's not our fault. His parents don't care. We fulfilled our duty by raising him for four months. That counts for something."

The old man saw his wife's infatuation and greatly disapproved. Although the two old people didn't have any children themselves, they usually cherished the child very much.

"His parents are perhaps dead; otherwise, they wouldn't be so heartless!"

"Dead? - I heard they got divorced, and neither of them wanted to raise the son."

"Oh heavens! What a sin! This kind of heart is unacceptable. There will be retribution in the future. So heartless!" The foster mother felt that the sins she was worried about should be the responsibility of his parents, so she felt a little more at ease.

"Conscience! When things are good, they only care about their own happiness. Once they have a falling out, they don't even care about the child. This is the game that modern young men and women play!"

The old man was angry with a hint of lament, the pupils deeply embedded in his eye sockets frozen.

"Then, where have they gone now? We should find them since the child has died, to avoid others gossiping."

"The man went abroad with his new wife, and the woman lives in Hankou with her lover. Are you going to find them? Even if you find them, they might not admit it."

The two fell silent. The night deepened in a sad loneliness. The child's corpse gradually became rigid. A kind of righteous indignation suddenly arose in the old woman's heart:

"If the child could grow up, he shouldn't acknowledge such parents either! They didn't put in any effort, only raised him for a short time!... Then what do we do with the child's body?"

"Call Little Sanzi tomorrow to testify."

Little Sanzi was the one who initially brought the child over. In the previous months, Little Sanzi brought a few dollars from his father every month, but in the past few months, Little Sanzi couldn't find his father either. Only after the child got sick did Little Sanzi say that his father had gone abroad and his mother had followed someone else. The old man initially feared that if the old woman knew this news, she would look down on the child, so he delayed telling her until today.

One of Mr. Du Jiutian's Calligraphy and Paintings 250

Mr. Du Jiutian of Shaoxing has been compiling science books at the Commercial Press for more than twenty years, and his writings are numerous. Appreciating art in his spare time, calligraphy, painting, and seal carving, although only secondary pursuits, are also remarkably admirable.

Page 25

The old woman selected some cleaner clothes to put on the child, sobbing as she continued until the dawn of the city.

Early in the morning, the old man called Little Sanzi. Little Sanzi sighed twice, then went to the charitable hall to get a small box, put the child's body inside. When the old man and Little Sanzi carried the small box out the door, the foster mother, who had been with him for a year, sobbed and said:

"It's not my fault, child. You can only blame your parents!"

In addition, the association's president, Mr. Bao Mingshan, has recently responded to the repeated requests of harmonica enthusiasts and will add a special harmonica class, specializing in the short-scale harmonica playing method, which is still the first of its kind in our country, and many other newly invented playing methods. It is also heard that at the same time, Mr. Bao will teach comrades from other places at the Huamei Radio Station in order to popularize this playing method. The classes are all taught by instructor Zheng Mo and President Bao. Those in this city who are interested in learning can go directly to the association's office at No. 11, Yuanchengli, Anren Street, Xinbeimen in the city to apply. (The Public)

Shen Bao Architectural Weekly

The Latest Composition of Residences (Part 2) 259

— Written by Kenichi Ichura, Translated by Guangzheng Zhang

However, the so-called air conditioning method involves delivering heated air with appropriate humidity into the room during winter, and delivering cooled air with reduced humidity into the room during summer. This is certainly very expensive, but also the most ideal. This method has recently been widely adopted in large commercial buildings, but its adoption in residences is still rare. Considering the importance of living, it is highly desirable that residences, schools, or offices can adopt it.

The initial means necessary for nighttime lighting was oil lamps. However, this has reached its peak and given way to the electric light era for the nighttime lives of all humanity. There was a temporary use of gas lamps in the past, but that is now history. It is foreseeable that they will not be able to usurp the position of electric lights in the future. There have also been various developments in the forms of electric lighting. However, indirect lighting, which is now generally considered ideal but has not yet become widespread, is not very popular due to economic reasons and the feeling of loneliness due to the lack of a light source elsewhere. It is likely that neon lighting will become popular in the future.

In addition to lighting, the uses of electricity in residences include power and fuel. The power required for various simple appliances is almost entirely supplied by electricity, and even more things have been electrified to date. For example, refrigerators, sewing machines, fans, vacuum cleaners, radios, clocks, washing, and the opening and closing of doors and windows, as well as transportation, all use electricity. On the other hand, electricity is used for cooking, irons, heating, and hot water supply.

Hot water supply has progressed from the original method of large-scale processing using boilers to the convenience of enjoying the widespread supply of gas water heaters and electric water heaters.

Hygiene equipment includes several types, such as sewage treatment, drainage, and waste and dust disposal. Among these, sewage treatment is the most important. Here, if public sewage ditches are well-constructed, it is very simple. However, as sewage ditches are still not widespread, each household has no other choice but to install septic tanks. These septic tanks have recently been simplified and made less expensive. Therefore, their construction does not require a large construction cost. Today, as drainage equipment is simplified, the proportion of hygiene equipment costs has gradually decreased, and it has also been gradually developed and improved.

The fuel for residences has been replaced by gas, which is now the most popular, instead of the former charcoal and coal. However, as mentioned earlier, it is destined to be replaced by electricity in the future. Indeed, while the sooty kitchens with charcoal have not completely disappeared, most of the cooking already uses gas. Although it is also widely used in irons, heating, cooling, and hot water supply, it has many shortcomings compared to electricity, except for its lower price.

In order to implement such equipment in residences, it is necessary to organically combine design and equipment to create a mutually rational system. Because this relies on the management of the entire project, it must be simple and unified. For example, the connection between the kitchen, heating room, and laundry room, as well as the connection between the bathroom, washroom, and toilet, can save area and reduce equipment costs. Therefore, from the perspective of practical living, design issues are particularly important.

For example, to improve the structure, a bathroom is installed upstairs. Because it is adjacent to the bedroom, there is no need for a dressing room. Also, if the toilet is placed in the bathroom, flushing is convenient and no sanitary efforts are required, and the appearance is not bad. In this way, a large area is saved, and the use is extremely easy. The laundry room might as well be located in the basement, equipped with an electric iron, which is also one of the home factories.

From an electrical perspective, if each room is in the appropriate location, electricity can be saved rationally. Electrical anti-theft equipment (automatic special doorbell) can also be created at a low price. The automatic adjustment of electric heating has also been gradually put into practical use recently and there is hope for its application.

The various types of equipment described above, regardless of their extremely complex mechanical structure, have very simple methods of use. However, conversely, it can also be said that their use must be paid considerable attention. That is to say, if general scientific knowledge does not advance, then these advanced equipment cannot be popularized. Because the use of these equipment shows that considerable scientific knowledge is necessary. Due to the steady progress of electrical equipment, the price of electricity will inevitably tend to decrease, which will make life more comfortable.

Residences are not only entrusted to construction, but also have related equipment. They are not only seen as machines for living, but also bear the responsibility of a complete living container. It is very gratifying to understand it this way. This complete living container has a solid and complete structure and a rational layout and design. These three companions depend on architects engaging in organic control to make them possible. (End)

Swedish Public Housing Architecture (Part 1) 260

— Buren

Currently, throughout Sweden, public apartments provide 22,000 residences, and the residents are mostly workers, merchants, partners, lower-level officials, and their families. In Stockholm alone, 600,000 people live in these apartments, accounting for 10% of the city's population. In other urban areas, there are more than ten places that imitate Stockholm's housing cooperative system, the largest of which are Gothenburg, Malmö, and Norrköping.

Sweden has spent 80,000,000 yuan on building houses nationwide. The development of housing construction has provided jobs for the unemployed and encouraged industry. At the same time, the living standards of most people have improved, and the health of countless elderly and children has been protected.

Swedish public apartments are called "Elephanthouses." Their tall and solemn appearance and the thoughtful and clean interior equipment are beyond the reach of public housing in other countries. Walking through the gate, visitors see a public playground, crowded with children. Along the paths, there are lawns, fences, and flowerbeds, neat and elegant, with public gardeners specializing in care.

There are 205 small apartments that accommodate two to four families. A gentle knock on the door will be answered, because the residents are happy to show their new homes to visitors. The bathroom has hot and cold water taps and a cosmetic cabinet. The kitchen has clean tableware, an electric refrigerator, a gas stove, and a white porcelain sink.

In the room, there is a bed and a couch. A table is placed in the center of the room, with books and vases on it. Looking from the door to the balcony, you can see flower baskets hanging from the ceiling. Blue awnings shield the sunlight. The bedroom is small, but Swedes are used to living in narrow houses. If the house is large, they will divide it into two.

The top floor of the apartment is a public nursery. Working women can leave their children here when they go out to work, entrusting them to well-trained nannies, and the cost is quite limited. The public nursery has a dining room and a library. Storytelling for one hour is one of the daily tasks. There is also a treatment room where children are treated if they have slight symptoms. The nursery is surrounded by a rooftop garden, which is most suitable for sunbathing and resting.

The equipment in the apartments is not simple, but it is based on the principle of not hindering convenience and comfort. The latest apartments are all built with steel and reinforced concrete and are equipped with automatic elevators. All electrical equipment that can replace manual labor is available. Each floor is equipped with an automatic waste conveyor. The windows and doors are made of single-piece "mirror glass," which does not obstruct the line of sight. When the windows and doors need to be washed, they can be rotated inward, so the washers do not have to stand on the window sills. Each floor is covered with painted cloth. Each residence is equipped with a wireless radio, which is indirectly broadcasted by the switchboard in the apartment.

There is also a kind of equipment installed in a small house, which can automatically clean carpets, mats, and other items. All residents must disinfect their furniture before moving in.

Research on Interior Lighting Distribution (Part 2) 261

— Qin

The source of light can be divided into two types: main and secondary. The former includes sunlight and lamplight, while the latter includes reflected light and light emitted by colors. Therefore, the application of interior paint is greatly related to the beauty of a room. If applied properly, it can adjust the deficiency of sunlight and lamplight, and its light often has a diffuse nature, without the disadvantage of dazzling the eyes, which is of great benefit to the interior decoration. Paint has different strengths of reflection of light. Light colors have strong reflection, while dark colors have weak reflection. To obtain a perfect color scheme, it is necessary to adjust paints of different strengths to achieve a suitable match. The following table shows the ratio of reflection of light for various colors, taking the reflection of magnesium oxide (98%) as the standard.

White ... 84.0%

Off-white ... 70.4%

Scarlet ... 69.4%

Ivory ... 64.3%

Yellow ... 60.5%

Flesh color ... 56.0%

Tan ... 55.4%

Light green ... 54.1%

Light gray ... 53.6%

Light blue ... 45.5%

Aluminum gray ... 41.9%

Brown ... 23.6%

Dark red ... 14.4%

Dark green ... 9.8%

Dark blue ... 9.3%

Black ... 10.0%

Reflected light is most suitable for interior light, but there are different kinds of reflected light. At the same time, the color matching must seek psychological comfort, and should not be too stimulating. There are three types of reflected light: (1) Specular reflection, in which the light travels along a certain straight line, that is, the angle of incidence must be equal to the angle of reflection. This kind of light has glare, which can easily cause strain on the eyes, so it is best to avoid it, such as light reflected from glass, polished metal surfaces, and mirrors. (2) Spread reflection, which is generally light reflected from metal surfaces or metal particles. Most of the light travels in the same direction, but not along the same straight line, so it appears spread after reflection. This can make the eyes slightly relaxed. (3) Diffuse reflection, which is the kind of light we need most. Its reflection comes from ordinary unpolished flat surfaces, such as white walls and ceilings. When light shines on this kind of flat surface, it is reflected and scattered in all directions, so it can make strong light not irritate the eyes, and achieve the requirement of brightness and pleasing to the eye.

From this point of view, if the coordination of light is to make it suitable for our residence and give full play to the beauty of the architecture, it is necessary to have a considerable understanding of the psychological influence and decorative value of various kinds of light. At the same time, it is necessary to make various colors obtain a balanced configuration according to the difference in their reflectivity. What is described here is only a brief discussion of the general situation. As for the coordination of light, the places where we usually rest, such as bedrooms, living rooms, and entertainment venues such as theaters, should use soft light and pleasing colors. Strong light and stimulating colors are suitable for places that make people excited, lively, and energetic. The color configuration in hospitals should be particularly studied, because it has a great impact on the psychology of patients, and special attention should be paid to the decoration of the ceiling. White light is not suitable for workplaces, and straw color or light green is more gentle. In offices, schools, shops, hotel lobbies, and special dining rooms, these places all require sufficient energy, agility, and liveliness, so the appropriate application of white has an indispensable value.
